Naqd and Mu‘āraḍah in Qiyas: The Hanafi Response
Defining naqd and mu‘āraḍah with examples and Hanafi responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a naqd argument in qiyas and explain the Hanafi method of specifying the ‘illah to preserve the analogy.

Core Idea
Naqd reveals the ‘illah must be refined; Hanafis permit takhṣīṣ to preserve analogy.

This passage introduces two critical objections in qiyas: naqd (refutation) and mu‘āraḍah (counter-evidence). The Hanafi school defends the validity of qiyas by showing that apparent contradictions can be resolved through specification (takhṣīṣ) of the effective cause. Understanding these tools is essential for evaluating analogical reasoning in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define naqd and its role in qiyas
Naqd occurs when the claimed ‘illah exists but the ruling does not. The text gives the example of wudu requiring intention as purification versus washing garments which are also purification but do not require intention.
Naqd is used by opponents to challenge the validity of the ‘illah.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to naqd
Hanafis respond by specifying the ‘illah: the true ‘illah is legal purification (ṭahārah ḥukmiyyah), which is not rationally understood and thus requires intention. Physical purification (washing garments) does not have this legal dimension.
This shows that takhṣīṣ al-‘illah is permissible in Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish mu‘āraḍah from naqd
Mu‘āraḍah is bringing another dalil that negates the ruling of the original proof without invalidating the proof itself. The text contrasts it with tanāquḍ (contradiction) which destroys the proof.
Mu‘āraḍah requires tarjīḥ (preponderance) to resolve.
4
Apply the concepts to the wudu example
The opponent argues: wudu is purification → intention required (like tayammum). Naqd: washing garments is also purification but no intention required. Hanafi response: the ‘illah is legal purification, not absolute purification. Thus the naqd is neutralized.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of refining the ‘illah.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute affects whether analogies can be saved by specifying the ‘illah. Hanafis allow it; Shafi‘i ahl al-ṭard do not, making more analogies invalid in their view.
This has implications for deriving rulings across fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه
قلنا: وصف كونه حراً قادراً يقتضي جواز النكاح، فلا يكون مؤثراً في عدم الجواز.
الناكح
وأما النقض فمثل ما يقال: الوضوء طهارة فيشترط له النية كالتيمم.
قلنا: ينقض بغسل الثوب والإناء.
وأما المعارَضَةُ فمثل ما يُقَال: المسحُ ركن في الوضوء فليسَنُ تثليثه كالغسل.
قلنا: المسحُ ركن فلا يُسَنُّ تثليثه كمسح الخفّ والتيمم.
في الوضوء
المسح
فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه:
الحكم يُتعلق بسببه، ويثبت بعلته، ويوجد عند شرطه.
الحكم
وأما النقض: فهو وجود العلة وتخلف الحكم عنه سواء كان لمانع أو لغيره عند من لم يجوز التخصيص أي: تخصيص العة، فالتخصيص مناقضة عندهم، وعند من جوزه هو تخلف الحكم عما ادعاه المعلل علة لا لمنانع، مثاله: ما يقال: الوضوء طهارة فيشترط فيه النية كالتيمم والجامع أن كلاً منهما عبادة ولا عبادة بدون النية، قلنا: ينقض يغسل الثوب والإناء لوجود العلة وهي الطهارة مع تخلف الحكم وهو اشتراط النية؛ لأنه لم يشترط النية فيهما فتدبر كذا قيل ما يقال إلخ القائلون هم أهل الطرد من الشافعية. [الشافي: ص ۲۸۲] قلنا : فعاد المعلل فارقاً بتغيير العلة إلى أن العلة ليست ما فهمتم حتى تقولوا: يلزم تخلف الحكم عن علة في طهارة الثوب، بل العلة عندنا هو الطهارة الحكمية وهي غير معقولة، فيحتاج فيها إلى النية، وأجاب عنه الحنفية بأن تنجس البدن بخروج النجاسة أمر معقول نعم الاقتصاء على الأعضاء الأربعة مع وجوب تطهير البدن كله غير معقول قد جوز لدفع الحرج، فإذا تنجس البدن والماء مطهر لطبيعة المطهر شرعاً أيضاً، فيتطهر به ويزيل النجاسة بلا حاجة إلى النية بخلاف التيمم، فإن التراب ملوث لا مطهر. وأمّا المعارَضَةُ : [الفرق بين التعارض والمتعارض أن التناقض يوجب بطلان نفس الدليل، والتعارض يمنع ثبوت الحكم من غير أن يتعرض الدليل] وهي أن يأتي السائل بدليل آخر ينفي حكم دليل المعلل بأن يقول للمعلل: ما ذكرت من الدليل وإن دل على الحكم، لكن عندنا من الدليل ما ينفيه. [حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٢٤٤]
Chapter on the cause of the ruling, its effective cause, and its condition. We say: The description of being free and capable necessitates the permissibility of marriage, so it is not effective in impermissibility. The married person. As for refutation (naqd), it is like when it is said: Wudu is purification, so intention is required for it, like tayammum. We say: It is refuted by washing a garment and a vessel. As for counter-evidence (mu‘āraḍah), it is like when it is said: Wiping is a pillar in wudu, so its triple repetition is not sunnah, like washing. We say: Wiping is a pillar, so its triple repetition is not sunnah, like wiping the khuff and tayammum. In wudu, wiping. Chapter on the cause of the ruling, its effective cause, and its condition: The ruling is attached to its cause, established by its effective cause, and exists at its condition. The ruling. As for refutation (naqd): it is the existence of the effective cause and the absence of the ruling from it, whether due to a preventer or not, according to those who do not permit specification (takhṣīṣ) i.e., specification of the cause; so specification is a contradiction according to them. According to those who permit it, it is the absence of the ruling from what the arguer claimed as an effective cause, without a preventer. Example: What is said: Wudu is purification, so intention is required in it like tayammum, and the common factor is that each is an act of worship and no act of worship is valid without intention. We say: It is refuted by washing a garment and a vessel, due to the existence of the effective cause (purification) along with the absence of the ruling (requirement of intention) because intention is not required in them. So reflect. It is said that those who say this are the people of rejection (ahl al-ṭard) from the Shafi‘is. [al-Shafi: p. 282] We say: The arguer then became a distinguisher by changing the effective cause to say that the effective cause is not what you understood, such that you could claim the absence of the ruling from an effective cause in the purification of a garment. Rather, the effective cause according to us is legal purification which is not rational, so intention is needed in it. The Hanafis responded by saying that the impurity of the body through the exit of filth is a rational matter. Indeed, limiting it to the four limbs while the entire body must be purified is not rational, but it is permitted to avoid hardship. So when the body becomes impure, water is a purifier by its nature and also legally a purifier, so one purifies with it and removes impurity without the need for intention, unlike tayammum, for earth is filthy not a purifier. As for counter-evidence (mu‘āraḍah): [The difference between contradiction and counter-evidence is that contradiction causes the invalidation of the proof itself, while counter-evidence prevents the establishment of the ruling without invalidating the proof.] It is that the questioner brings another proof that negates the ruling of the arguer's proof, by saying to the arguer: The proof you mentioned, even if it indicates the ruling, we have proof that negates it. [Margin of Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p. 244]
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of two important concepts in the methodology of qiyas (analogical reasoning): naqd (refutation) and mu‘āraḍah (counter-evidence). The text begins with the definition of naqd: it is the existence of the claimed ‘illah (effective cause) while the ruling is absent, either due to a preventer (mani‘) or not, depending on one's stance on takhṣīṣ (specification) of the ‘illah. Those who do not allow takhṣīṣ consider this a contradiction (munāqaḍah). The example given is the claim that wudu requires intention because it is purification, akin to tayammum. The Hanafi refutation (naqd) points out that washing a garment and a vessel also involve purification but do not require intention, so the ‘illah is present yet the ruling is absent. The Hanafi response then refines the ‘illah: the true ‘illah is 'legal purification' (ṭahārah ḥukmiyyah), which is not rationally understood, unlike physical purification. This leads into a further discussion distinguishing the types of purification. The mu‘āraḍah discussion defines it as the opponent bringing another dalil that negates the ruling of the original dalil, without necessarily invalidating the original dalil itself. The text clarifies the difference between tanāquḍ (contradiction, which invalidates the proof) and ta‘āruḍ (counter-evidence, which merely prevents the ruling from being established). Throughout, the Hanafi position is presented and defended against the Shafi‘i 'ahl al-ṭard' (people of rejection). The passage should be understood as part of the broader usul al-fiqh debate on the validity and limits of qiyas.

Key Terms
النقض (al-naqd): The existence of the claimed effective cause (‘illah) while the ruling is absent, either due to a preventer or not, used as a refutation of the analogy.
المعارضة (al-mu‘āraḍah): Bringing another proof (dalil) that negates the ruling of the original proof, without necessarily invalidating the original proof itself.
العلة (al-‘illah): The effective cause that necessitates the ruling; in this context, it is the attribute that is claimed to be the reason for the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between naqd and mu‘āraḍah as explained in the passage?
A) Naqd invalidates the proof, while mu‘āraḍah prevents the ruling from being established without invalidating the proof.
B) Naqd is bringing another proof, while mu‘āraḍah is showing the absence of the ruling despite the existence of the ‘illah.
C) Naqd is specific to wudu, while mu‘āraḍah is specific to tayammum.
D) There is no difference; they are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
Naqd in qiyas is not necessarily fatal; the Hanafi school permits takhṣīṣ of the ‘illah to resolve apparent contradictions and preserve analogical reasoning.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Four Factors of a Ruling: Cause, Effective Cause, Condition, and Sign
Defines and exemplifies four categories of factors related to rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cause (sabab), effective cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign ('alama) and apply the Hanafi rule of attributing rulings to these factors.

Core Idea
The ruling is attributed to the effective cause when present; only when impossible does it shift to the cause, then to the condition.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, rulings are tied to certain factors. This passage presents a rigorous classification: cause (sabab), effective cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign ('alama). Each plays a distinct role in the existence and attribution of legal rulings. You will learn not only their definitions but also the hierarchical rule that determines which factor the ruling is attributed to when multiple are present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four factors
Read the definitions given for sabab, 'illa, shart, and 'alama. Note that sabab leads to the ruling via an intermediary (the 'illa), while 'illa inherently necessitates the ruling. Shart is a prerequisite without leading or necessitating, and 'alama is a mere indicator.
The everyday examples (road, rope) help anchor the concept of 'pathway via intermediary'.
2
Analyze the attribution rule
The core rule: when both sabab and 'illa are present, the ruling is attributed to the 'illa. Only when attribution to the 'illa is impossible (e.g., the 'illa is not directly attributable) does it go to the sabab. This rule is then extended to shart and 'alama in the hierarchy.
The examples of liability (knife, boy, animal) illustrate how this rule determines legal responsibility.
3
Examine the fiqhi examples
Work through the examples: (1) lifting a knife to a boy who kills himself – no liability because the boy's voluntary act is the effective cause; (2) knife falling from boy's hand – liability because no voluntary act intervenes, so attribution to cause; (3) mounting a boy on an animal and it moves – no liability due to boy's voluntary sitting; (4) directing someone to steal or kill – no liability for the director because the directed person's act is the effective cause.
These examples show how the attribution rule is applied in practice.
4
Apply the hierarchy
The passage concludes with a hierarchy: default attribution to effective cause; if impossible, to cause; if impossible, to condition; and sometimes to other factors (e.g., supererogatory prayers attributed to the act itself). Understand this hierarchy by considering examples like asr prayer (attributed to time as effective cause), sadaqat al-fitr (attributed to condition of moon sighting).
The hierarchy is not absolute; some rulings are attributed outside this scheme (e.g., nafl prayers).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه
فالسبب ما يكون طريقاً إلى الشيء بواسطة، كالطريق، فإنه سبب للوصول إلى المقصد بواسطة المشي، والحَبْل سَبَب للوصول إلى الماء بالإدلاء.
فعلى هذا: كل ما كان طريقا إلى الحكم بواسطة يسمى سبباً لــه شرعاً، ويسمى الواسطة علةً.
مثاله: فتح باب الإصطبل، والقفص، وحل قيد العبد، فإنه سبب للتلف بواسطة توجد من الدابة والطيز والعبد
والسبَبُ مع العلة إذا اجتَمَعَا يضاف الحكمُ إلى العلة دون السبب، إلا إذا تعذرت الإضافة إلى العلة فيضاف إلى السبب حينئذ.
وعلى هذا قال أصحابنا: إذا رفع السكين إلى صبي فقتل به نفسه لا يضمن، ولو سَقَط السكين من يد الصبي فجَرَحَه يضمن، ولو حَمَلَ الصبيَّ على دابَّة فسيَّرَها فحالت يُمْنَةً الدابة مالت ويسرةً فسقط ومات لا يضمن ولو دلَّ إنساناً على مال الغير فسَرَقَه، أو على نفسه الصبي فقتله، أو على قافلة فقطعَ عليهم الطريق لا يجب الضمان على الدَّال.
واعلم أن ما يتعلق به الأحكام أربعة: السبب والعلة والشرط، والعلامة، ووجه الحصر على هذه الأربعة: أن ما يتعلق به الأحكام إما مؤثر في الحكم ووجوده ظاهراً أو لا يكون، فالأول هو "العلة"، والثاني إما يوجد الحكم عنده أم لا ، فالأول هو الشرط"، والثاني إما أن يكون علماً على وجود الحكم أو لا، فالأول "العلامة" والثاني هو "السبب"، وإلا أن يحمل دليل الحصر على الاستقرار.
والحاصل أن ما فيه افضاء لا اقتضاء هو "السبب" وما فيه اقتضاء للحكم أيضاً بذاته أي: ما يقتضيه بطبعه هو "العلة"، وما ليس فيه افضاء ولا اقتضاء بل لوجوده دخل في تحقق الحكم بأنه منوط به وموقوف عليه هو "الشرط"، وما ليس له دخل أيضاً بل مجرد تعريف وكشف هو "العلامة والإمارة"، والأصل في إضافة الحكم أن يضاف إلى "علة" كصلاة العصر، وإذا تعذرت فإلى "العلة" كالسوق والقود، وعند التعذر فإلى "السبب المحض، وعند التعذر فإلى "الشرط" كصدقة الفطر وحجة الإسلام، وقد يضاف إلى غيرها كصلاة التسبيح، وصلاة الإستخارة، وصلاة القضاء والنفل فافهم.
والسبَبُ مع العلة إذا اجتَمَعَا يضاف الحكمُ إلى العلة دون السبب، إلا إذا تعذرت الإضافة إلى العلة فيضاف إلى السبب حينئذ.
وعلى هذا قال أصحابنا: إذا رفع السكين إلى صبي فقتل به نفسه لا يضمن، ولو سَقَط السكين من يد الصبي فجَرَحَه يضمن، ولو حَمَلَ الصبيَّ على دابَّة فسيَّرَها فحالت يُمْنَةً الدابة مالت ويسرةً فسقط ومات لا يضمن ولو دلَّ إنساناً على مال الغير فسَرَقَه، أو على نفسه الصبي فقتله، أو على قافلة فقطعَ عليهم الطريق لا يجب الضمان على الدَّال.
The fourth research topic: On Qiyas. Chapter on the cause of the ruling, its effective cause, and its condition. The cause is that which is a pathway to a thing via an intermediary, like a road—it is a cause for reaching the destination via walking, and a rope is a cause for reaching water by lowering. Based on this: everything that is a pathway to a ruling via an intermediary is called a cause in the Shari'a, and the intermediary is called the effective cause. Example: opening the door of a stable or cage, and untying the slave's fetter—it is a cause for destruction via an intermediary that occurs from the animal, bird, or slave. The cause and the effective cause when together, the ruling is attributed to the effective cause, not the cause, except when attribution to the effective cause is impossible, then it is attributed to the cause at that time. Based on this, our companions said: if he lifts a knife to a boy and the boy kills himself with it, he is not liable; if the knife fell from the boy's hand and injured him, he is liable; if he mounted a boy on an animal and set it moving, and the animal leaned right and left, and the boy fell and died, he is not liable; if he directed someone to another's property and he stole it, or to himself and he killed him, or to a caravan and they were robbed, liability is not due on the director. Know that the things related to rulings are four: cause, effective cause, condition, and sign. The reason for limitation to these four is: that which is related to rulings is either effective in the ruling and its existence is manifest, or not. The first is the effective cause. The second: either the ruling exists with it or not; the first is the condition, and the second: either it is a sign of the existence of the ruling or not; the first is the sign and the second is the cause, unless the evidence of limitation is interpreted as stabilization. In summary: that which has leading without requiring is the cause; that which inherently requires the ruling is the effective cause; that which has neither leading nor requiring but its existence has a role in the realization of the ruling—being contingent upon it—is the condition; and that which has no role beyond mere definition and disclosure is the sign and indicator. The principle in attributing the ruling is to attribute it to the effective cause, as in the afternoon prayer; if that is impossible, then to the effective cause? (as in market and qisas); when impossible, then to the pure cause; when impossible, then to the condition, as in sadaqat al-fitr and the pilgrimage; and it is sometimes attributed to other than these, as in prayer of tasbih, prayer of istikhara, prayer of qada and optional prayers—so understand.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This is a foundational passage in Hanafi usul al-fiqh explaining four categories of factors related to legal rulings: cause (sabab), effective cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign ('alama). The author opens by defining cause as a pathway to a ruling via an intermediary, using everyday examples like a road (cause) to a destination via walking (intermediary). In Shari'a, the intermediary is called the effective cause. Then he gives a fiqhi example: opening a stable door (cause) leads to the animal escaping (intermediary/effective cause) and thus destruction. The key rule: when both cause and effective cause are present, the ruling is attributed to the effective cause, not the cause. Exceptions occur when attribution to the effective cause is impossible—then the ruling goes to the cause. Five examples from Hanafi jurisprudence illustrate this rule: (1) Lifting a knife to a boy who then kills himself: the doer is not liable because the direct act (the effective cause) is the boy's own voluntary act; (2) If the knife falls from the boy's hand and injures him, the doer is liable because the falling is not the boy's voluntary act, so attribution goes to the cause; (3) Mounting a boy on an animal and it moves causing fall: not liable because the boy's voluntary act (sitting) intervenes; (4) Directing someone to steal or kill: the director is not liable because the directed person's voluntary act is the effective cause. The passage then systematically distinguishes the four categories: effective cause (inherently necessitates the ruling), cause (leads to ruling without necessitating), condition (prerequisite without leading or necessitating), and sign (mere indicator). The default attribution hierarchy is: effective cause → then if impossible, to the cause → then to the condition. Examples given: asr prayer attributed to time (effective cause), market/qisas to effective cause? (though text says 'illa perhaps meaning sunnah or ruling), sadaqat al-fitr attributed to condition (sighting of moon), Hajj to condition (ability). Additional examples of attributions to other factors include supererogatory prayers.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): That which is a pathway to the ruling via an intermediary; it has leading (ifda') but not requiring (iqtida').
العلة (al-'illa): The intermediary that inherently necessitates the ruling; it is effective in the ruling.
الشرط (al-shart): That which has no leading or requiring but its existence is necessary for the realization of the ruling.
العلامة (al-'alama): A mere indicator of the existence of the ruling, without any role in causing or conditioning it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule stated in this passage, when both the cause (sabab) and the effective cause ('illa) are present, to which is the ruling attributed?
A) The cause (sabab)
B) The effective cause ('illa)
C) The condition (shart)
D) The sign ('alama)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the ruling is primarily attributed to the effective cause; only when that is impossible does attribution shift to the cause, then to the condition, and the sign is merely indicative.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Attribution of Ruling to Sabab vs Illah (Usul al-Shashi)
Principle stating when ruling is attributed to illah over sabab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when sabab and illah combine, the ruling is attributed to the illah except when attribution is impossible, and distinguish the exceptional cases where the sabab functions as illah.

Core Idea
The illah governs the ruling; the sabab only when the illah cannot.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi addresses a fundamental question in legal reasoning: when two causes are present—a sabab (occasion) and an illah (effective cause)—which one determines the ruling? The answer is central to understanding how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from causes. Using concrete examples ranging from knife incidents to directions, the author illustrates the principle and its exception, and even touches on a scholarly dispute regarding classification. Mastering this rule sharpens your ability to analyze causation in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the principle and its exception
The text states: when sabab and illah combine, the ruling is attributed to the illah; only when attribution to the illah is impossible, it goes to the sabab.
Memorize this rule: 'يضاف الحكم إلى العلة دون السبب، إلا إذا تعذرت الإضافة إلى العلة'.
2
Understand the rationale
The illah directly influences and establishes the ruling; the sabab merely leads to it, so the illah takes priority.
This is based on the definition of illah as the effective cause.
3
Examine the five illustrative cases
For each case (knife to boy, knife falls, boy on beast, directing to steal, directing to kill), identify the sabab and illah, and determine why the ruling is attributed to the illah (or to the sabab in the falling knife case).
The falling knife case is the exception where attribution to the illah is impossible because the boy's act is not voluntary.
4
Analyze the two exceptional cases (depositor and pilgrim)
In these, the sabab itself becomes the basis of liability because it involves a breach of obligation (depositor) or a prohibited act (pilgrim). Here the sabab functions like an illah.
The ruling is attributed to the sabab, not because the illah is impossible, but because the sabab itself is the effective cause.
5
Consider the terminological dispute with al-Manar
The author of al-Manar classifies causes like purchase of a relative as illah, while al-Shashi classifies them as sabab. This affects rulings on manumission when the purchase is invalid.
Al-Manar gives priority to the aspect of effectiveness (illiyya); al-Shashi to the aspect of causality (sababiyya).

Source Text

البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه
والسبَبُ مع العلة إذا اجتَمَعَا يضاف الحكمُ إلى العلة دون السبب، إلا إذا تعذرت الإضافة إلى العلة فيضاف إلى السبب حينئذ.
وعلى هذا قال أصحابنا له إذا رفع السكين إلى صبي فقتل به نفسه لا يضمن، ولو سقط السكين من يد الصبي فجَرَحَه يضمن، ولو حَمَلَ الصبيَّ على دابَّة فسيَّرَها فحالت يُمْنَةً الدابة مالت ويسرةً فسقط ومات لا يضمن ولو دلَّ إنساناً على مال الغير فسَرَقَه، أو على نفسه الصبي فقتله، أو على قافلة فقطعَ عليهم الطريق لا يجب الضمان على الدَّال.
الحكم إلى العلة لأنها تؤثر في الحكم وتثبت بها، والسبب يفضي إليه أي إلى الحكم لا غير، فكانت أولى بإضافته إليها، فلا يضمن الفاتح قيمة الدابة والطير ولا الحال قيمة الدابة والطير ولا الحال قيمة العبد في الصورة المذكورة كذا في بعض الحواشي لا يضمنُ إلى أي دية قتله بناء على أن دفعه سبب لقتله، وإنما لا يضمنه؛ لأن موته مضاف إلى فعله باختياره وهو صالح لإضافة الحكم إليه؛ لكونه اختيارياً، فلا يكون مضافاً إلى السبب بعد صلاحيته لإضافته إلى علته الحقيقية.
الدابة وهو يضمن أي الدافع؛ لأن سقوط السكين ليس بفعل اختياري له فلم يكن الهلاك حاصلاً بمباشرة فعل الإهلاك اختياراً بل بامساكه الذي هو حكم دفع الدافع وهو متعد في الدفع، فيضاف ما لزم من الإمساك إليه، فصار الدفع سبباً لحكم العلة باعتبار أن علة التلف وهي سقوط السكين عن الصبي مما تعذرت الإضافة إليها؛ لأنه ليس بفعله اختياراً كذا في "المعدن" و "الفصول". لا يضمن أي الحامل؛ لأن الحمل وإن كان سبباً لتلفه هو الصبي) لكن اعترضت عليه علة وهي سير فعل اختياري للصبي، فيضاف إلى العلة، وأما إذا سيرها الحامل فسقط الصبي ومات يضمن الحامل؛ لأن السقوط يضاف إليه فافهم كذا في "المعدن". لا يجب الضمان إلخ لأن الدلالة سبب محض؛ إذ هي طريق الوصول إلى المقصود، وقد تحلل بينهما أي بين السبب والحكم علة تصلح إضافة الحكم إليها، وهي فعل المدلول الذي يباشره باختيار فيضاف إليها، فهذه المسائل الخمس المتفرعة على الأصل المذكور، وهو أن السبب والعلة إذا اجتمعا يضاف الحكم إلى العلة إلا في مسألة سقوط السكين، فإنها أضيف حكمها إلى السبب وهي متفرعة على الاستثناء بقوله: إلا إذا تعذرت الإضافة إلخ كذا في "المعدن".
وهذا بخلاف المودع إذا دلَّ السَّارق على الوديعة فَسَرَقَهَا أو دل الْمُحْرِمُ غيره على صيد الحرم فقتله؛ لأن وجوب الضمان على المودع باعتبار ترك الحفظ الواجب عليه لا بالدلالة وعلى المحرم باعتبار أن الدلالة محظور إحرامه بمنزلة مس الطيب ولبس للمخيط فيضمن بارتكاب المحظور لا بالدلالة، إلا أن الجناية إنما تتقرر بحقيقة القتل، فأما قبله فلا حكم له الجواز ارتفاع أثر الجناية بمنزلة الاندمال في باب الجراحة.
وقد يكون السبب بمعنى العلة، فيضاف الحكم إليه.
ذلك بخلاف المودع إلخ: جواب سوال، وهو: أن دالة المودع والمحرم أيضاً سبب محض لدلالة السارق، ومع أضيف الحكم إلى السبب يعني يجب الضمان ههنا على المودع والمحرم وحاصل الجواب: أن الضمان على المودع إنما هو بجناية على مال الوديعة وهو ترك الحفظ الذي التزمه بعقد الوديعة، فكان ضامناً مباشرة هذه الجناية بنفسه دون أن يضمن بفعل المدلول مضافاً إليه بطريق التسبيب وأن الضمان على المحرم إنما يجب باعتبار أن الدلالة إلخ كذا في "المعدن". إلا أن الجناية إلخ جواب سوال وهو: أنه لو كان الضمان على المحرم باعتبار ارتكاب مخظور يجب عليه الضمان بمجرد الدلالة بدون أن يتصل بالقتل، فأجاب بأن الجناية إنما يوجب تقرر إلخ كذا في "المعدن". بمنزلة الاندمال وهو كون الجراحة بعد البرء بحال لا يرى أثر الشين فيها بسبب الالتمام، فهو يوجب ارتفاع الضمان من الجاني، ولهذا عده الاندمال من موانع الحكم. بحقيقة القتل: لأن الدلالة إنما صارت جناية بإزالته أمن الصيد، وإزالة بعرض الانتقال والانتقاض أي: بقرب انتقال إزالة الأمن وانتقاضها لجواز إلخ. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ٢٢٥]
إحرامه وهو الدالة أن
وقد يكون السبب إلخ: جعله صاحب "المنار" علة في خير الأسباب لها شبهة بالأسباب، ومثله بشراء القريب ومرض الموت والشركية عند الأيام، وكذا كل ما هو علة العلة، فعده المصنف له من قسم الأسباب فيرجح فيه جهة السببية على جهة العلية، وصاحب "المنار" عده من قسم العلل، فترجح عنده جهة العلية فيه على جهة السببية، ثم كل تقدير يجب في علة إذا أضيف الحكم إليها أن يتعذر إضافته إلى العلة فإنه الأصل، فعند الأصل يسقط الخلف، وقد يقال: إن العلة في العتق ليست هو الملك والشراء علة للملك بل العلة للعتق وهو مجموع الملك والقرابة، لكن لما كان الملك هو الجزء الآخير للعلة أضيف إليه الحكم كذا في "الحصول".
Fourth Investigation: On Analogy. Chapter on the cause of the ruling, its effective cause, and its condition. The cause (sabab) and the effective cause (illah) when they combine, the ruling is attributed to the effective cause, not the cause, except when attribution to the effective cause is impossible, then it is attributed to the cause at that time. And according to this, our companions said: if someone raises a knife to a boy and the boy kills himself with it, he is not liable; and if the knife falls from the boy's hand and wounds him, he is liable; and if someone carries a boy on a beast and makes it go, and it swerves right and left so that he falls and dies, he is not liable; and if someone directs a person to another's property and he steals it, or to a boy and he kills him, or to a caravan and they are robbed on the road, liability is not required from the director. The ruling (is attributed) to the effective cause because it influences the ruling and is established by it, while the cause leads to it, i.e., to the ruling, nothing else, so it is more deserving to be attributed to it. Thus the opener is not liable for the value of the beast and the bird, nor the mover for the value of the beast and the bird, nor the mover for the value of the slave in the mentioned scenario, as in some glosses: he is not liable for any blood money for killing him, based on the fact that his pushing is a cause for his killing. And he is not liable because his death is attributed to his own act by choice, and he is suitable for attribution of the ruling to him because it is voluntary; so it is not attributed to the cause after it is suitable to be attributed to its true effective cause. The beast: and he is liable, i.e., the pusher, because the fall of the knife is not a voluntary act of his, so destruction did not occur by directly performing the act of destruction voluntarily, but by his holding which is the ruling of the pusher's push, and he is transgressing in pushing, so whatever results from holding is attributed to him. So the push became a cause for the ruling of the effective cause, considering that the effective cause of destruction, i.e., the knife falling from the boy, could not be attributed to him because it is not his voluntary act, as in al-Ma'din and al-Fusul. He is not liable, i.e., the carrier, because although carrying is a cause for his destruction (the boy), an effective cause intervenes, i.e., the movement is a voluntary act of the boy, so it is attributed to the effective cause. But if the carrier makes it go and the boy falls and dies, the carrier is liable because the fall is attributed to him; understand, as in al-Ma'din. Liability is not required etc. because directing is a pure cause, since it is the means of reaching the goal, and between them, i.e., between the cause and the ruling, there intervenes an effective cause that is suitable for attributing the ruling to it, i.e., the act of the directed person which he performs voluntarily, so it is attributed to it. These five issues branch from the mentioned principle, which is that when cause and effective cause combine, the ruling is attributed to the effective cause, except in the case of the falling knife, where its ruling was attributed to the cause, and that branches from the exception in his statement: except when attribution is impossible, etc., as in al-Ma'din. And this is contrary to the depositor if he directs the thief to the deposit and he steals it, or if the pilgrim (muhrim) directs another to a game animal in the sanctuary and he kills it; because the obligation of liability upon the depositor is due to his failure to safeguard which was obligatory upon him, not due to the direction; and upon the pilgrim because direction is a prohibited act of his state of ihram, akin to applying perfume and wearing sewn garments, so he is liable for committing the prohibited act, not for the direction. However, the offense (jinaaya) is only established by the actual killing; before that, it has no ruling, and the possibility of removing the effect of the offense is like the healing (indimaal) in the chapter of wounds. And sometimes the cause (sabab) is in the meaning of effective cause (illah), so the ruling is attributed to it. That (the previous) is contrary to the depositor etc.: this is the answer to a question: that the direction of the depositor and the pilgrim is also a pure cause for the direction of the thief, and yet the ruling is attributed to the cause, meaning that liability is required here upon the depositor and the pilgrim. The summary of the answer: that the liability upon the depositor is due to an offense against the property of the deposit, i.e., abandoning the safeguard which he undertook by the deposit contract, so he is liable for directly committing this offense himself, without being liable for the act of the directed person attributed to him by way of causing; and that the liability upon the pilgrim is necessarily due to the fact that the direction is prohibited, etc., as in al-Ma'din. However, the offense etc. is the answer to a question: that if liability were upon the pilgrim due to committing a prohibited act, he would be liable merely by the direction without connection to the killing. He answered that the offense only necessitates establishment, etc., as in al-Ma'din. Like indimaal, which is the wound healing after recovery such that no trace of injury remains due to closure; it necessitates removal of liability from the perpetrator, and for this reason indimaal is counted among the preventers of the ruling. By actual killing: because the direction only becomes an offense by removing the security of the game animal, and removal is vulnerable to transfer and nullification, i.e., due to the nearness of transfer and nullification of removal of security because of possibility, etc. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 225]. His state of ihram: the one directing that. And sometimes the cause etc.: the author of al-Manar considered it an effective cause in the best of causes having resemblance to causes; examples include buying a relative, illness of death, and partnership during days, and likewise everything that is the cause of the cause. The author (of al-Shashi) classified it as a type of cause, so the aspect of causality (sababiyya) outweighs the aspect of effectiveness (illiyya). The author of al-Manar classified it as a type of effective cause, so at his view the aspect of effectiveness outweighs the aspect of causality. Then, every estimation of an effective cause requires that if the ruling is attributed to it, attribution to the effective cause becomes impossible, for that is the principle. According to the principle, the difference collapses. And it may be said: the effective cause in manumission is not ownership alone; purchase is the cause of ownership, but the effective cause for manumission is the combination of ownership and kinship. However, since ownership is the last part of the effective cause, the ruling is attributed to it, as in al-Husul.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage from the fourth chapter of Usul al-Shashi, on qiyas, presents a key usul principle regarding the attribution of a legal ruling when both a sabab (cause/occasion) and an illah (effective cause) are present. The author begins by stating the rule: when sabab and illah come together, the ruling is attributed to the illah, not the sabab, unless attribution to the illah is impossible, in which case it goes to the sabab. The reasoning is that the illah directly influences and establishes the ruling, while the sabab merely leads to it. Five illustrative examples from Hanafi fiqh follow. 1) If a person lifts a knife to a boy and the boy kills himself, the lifter is not liable because the death is attributed to the boy's own voluntary act (illah). 2) If the knife falls from the boy's hand and injures him, the lifter is liable because the fall is not a voluntary act of the boy; thus attribution to the illah (the boy's act) is impossible, so it goes to the sabab (the lifter's act). 3) If a person puts a boy on an animal and the boy makes it move and falls, the carrier is not liable—the boy's voluntary act is the illah. 4) If a person directs someone to another's property and he steals it, the director is not liable—the thief's voluntary act is the illah. 5) Similarly, directing to kill or rob a caravan—the actor's voluntary act is the illah. The text then elaborates on the exception (the falling knife case) where attribution to the illah is impossible. The second page contrasts these with two cases where the ruling is attributed to the sabab despite the presence of an illah-like act: the depositor who directs a thief to the deposit (liability is due to his own breach of trust, not the direction) and the pilgrim in ihram who directs someone to game (liability is due to his prohibited act of directing, which is akin to other ihram violations). The text clarifies that here the sabab itself takes on the role of the illah. Finally, it notes a terminological dispute: the author of al-Manar considers certain causes (like buying a relative that leads to manumission) as illah, while the author of al-Shashi classifies them as sabab. The passage is fundamental for understanding how Hanafi usul distinguishes between the occasion and the effective cause in attributing rulings, particularly in cases of indirect causation.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause or occasion that leads to the ruling but does not directly influence it; it is the means or pathway to the ruling.
علة (illah): The effective cause that directly influences the ruling and is the basis for its establishment; it is the true rationale behind the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when both sabab and illah are present, to which is the ruling attributed?
A) The sabab, because it is the cause.
B) The illah, because it directly influences the ruling.
C) Both equally.
D) Neither, the ruling stands alone.

Key Takeaway
The ruling is attributed to the illah whenever possible; only when the illah cannot be attributed does the sabab take effect, and in some cases the sabab itself functions as the illah.

Distinguishing Sabab, 'Illa, and Shart in Qiyas
Explaining the distinction between sabab, 'illa, and shart with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sabab and 'illa in Hanafi usul and apply the classification to examples of causation and liability.

Core Idea
A pure sabab does not attract liability unless it is treated as 'illa or the agent is compelled.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, we explore the critical Hanafi distinction between sabab (cause) and 'illa (effective cause) within qiyas. The text uses vivid examples—like the depositary guiding a thief or the muhrim guiding a hunter—to show when liability arises from a cause directly or indirectly. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying qiyas and determining legal responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of sabab
According to Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi, sabab is divided into pure sabab (like digging a well), figurative sabab (like an oath), and sabab that functions as 'illa (like driving an animal).
The third category is where sabab is treated as 'illa when attribution to the real 'illa is impossible.
2
Distinguish between pure sabab and sabab with semblance of 'illa
Pure sabab only triggers a ruling if the person has a direct duty (e.g., depositary's duty to preserve). Sabab with semblance of 'illa transfers liability to the cause when the immediate actor is compelled.
Example: the driver is liable because the animal is coerced; the witness is liable because the judge is compelled by testimony.
3
Analyze the examples of depositary and muhrim
The depositary is liable for neglecting his duty, not for the guidance itself. The muhrim is liable for violating ihram prohibitions, even though the killing is by another.
This shows that pure sabab alone does not create liability; there must be a direct violation of a duty or a prohibited act.
4
Examine the madhhab dispute on tazkiya
Imam Abu Hanifa holds attestors liable if they retract, because their praise enabled the judge's ruling. The Sahibayn disagree, arguing that praise is not a cause of loss.
The dispute illustrates how classification of an act as pure sabab vs. sabab with 'illa affects legal outcomes.
5
Apply the distinction to the attribution of the judge's ruling
The judge's ruling is attributed to the witness's testimony because the judge is considered compelled after hearing just testimony; similarly, the animal's act is attributed to the driver.
This is a key principle: when the immediate actor is legally compelled, the cause stands in for the 'illa.

البحث الرابع في القياس فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه وهذا بخلاف المودع إذا دلَّ السَّارق على الوديعة فَسَرَقَهَا أو دل الْمُحْرِمُ غيره على صيد الحرم فقتله؛ لأن وجوب الضمان على المودع باعتبار ترك الحفظ الواجب عليه لا بالدلالة به عليه وعلى المحرم باعتبار أن الدلالة محظور إحرامه بمنزلة مس الطيب ولبس للمخيط القتل فيضمن بارتكاب المحظور لا بالدلالة، إلا أن الجناية إنما تتقرر بحقيقة القتل، فأما قبله فلا حكم له الجواز ارتفاع أثر الجناية بمنزلة الاندمال في باب الجراحة. وقد يكون السبب بمعنى العلة، فيضاف الحكم إليه. ذلك بخلاف المودع إلخ: جواب سوال، وهو: أن دالة المودع والمحرم أيضاً سبب محض لدلالة السارق، ومع أضيف الحكم إلى السبب يعني يجب الضمان ههنا على المودع والمحرم وحاصل الجواب: أن الضمان على المودع إنما هو بجناية على مال الوديعة وهو ترك الحفظ الذي التزمه بعقد الوديعة، فكان ضامناً مباشرة هذه الجناية بنفسه دون أن يضمن بفعل المدلول مضافاً إليه بطريق التسبيب وأن الضمان على المحرم إنما يجب باعتبار أن الدلالة إلخ كذا في "المعدن". إلا أن الجناية إلخ جواب سوال وهو: أنه لو كان الضمان على المحرم باعتبار ارتكاب مخظور يجب عليه الضمان بمجرد الدلالة بدون أن يتصل بالقتل، فأجاب بأن الجناية إنما يوجب تقرر إلخ كذا في "المعدن". بمنزلة الاندمال وهو كون الجراحة بعد البرء بحال لا يرى أثر الشين فيها بسبب الالتمام، فهو يوجب ارتفاع الضمان من الجاني، ولهذا عده الاندمال من موانع الحكم. بحقيقة القتل: لأن الدلالة إنما صارت جناية بإزالته أمن الصيد، وإزالة بعرض الانتقال والانتقاض أي: بقرب انتقال إزالة الأمن وانتقاضها لجواز إلخ. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ٢٢٥] إحرامه وهو الدالة[؟] أن وقد يكون السبب إلخ: جعله صاحب "المنار" علة في خير الأسباب لها شبهة بالأسباب، ومثله بشراء القريب ومرض الموت والشركية عند الأيام، وكذا كل ما هو علة العلة، فعده المصنف له من قسم الأسباب فيرجح فيه جهة السببية على جهة العلية، وصاحب "المنار" عده من قسم العلل، فترجح عنده جهة العلية فيه على جهة السببية، ثم كل تقدير يجب في علة إذا أضيف الحكم إليها أن يتعذر إضافته إلى العلة فإنه الأصل، فعند الأصل يسقط الخلف، وقد يقال: إن العلة في العتق ليست هو الملك والشراء علة للملك بل العلة للعتق وهو مجموع الملك والقرابة، لكن لما كان الملك هو الجزء الآخير للعلة أضيف إليه الحكم كذا في "الحصول". ومثاله: فيما يثبت العلةُ بالسبب، فيكون السبب في معنى العلة؛ لأنه لما ثبت العلةُ كون السبب بمعنى العلة بالسبب فيكون السبب في معنى علة العلة، فيُضاف الحكم إليه. السبب ولهذا قلنا: إذا ساق دابَّةً فأتلف شيئًا ضمن السائق. والشاهدُ إذا أتلف بشهادته مالاً فظَهَرَ بطلانها بالرجوع ضمن؛ لأن سير الدابَّة يضاف إلى السوق. وقضاء القاضي يُضاف إلى الشهادة؛ لما أنَّه لا يسعه ترك القضاء بعد ظهور الحق بشهادة العدل عنده، فيكون السبب : اعلم أن حافظ الدين النسفي قسم السبب إلى سبب محض ليس له شبهة العلية كحفر البئر، والدلالة على مال إنسان أو نفسه، وإلى سبب مجازي له شبهة العلة كاليمين للكفارة وتعليق الطلاق والعتاق للوقوع، وإلى سبب في الحكم العلة كعلة العلة عند تعذر الإضافة أي العلة كالسوق والقود، فأعتبر الأخير من الأسباب أيضاً، وقسم العلة إلى سبعة أقسام اسماً وحكماً ومعني. ضمن السائقُ لأن إصابة يدها بذهابها وإن كان علة للتلف لكنها حدثت بالسوق؛ لأن السوق يحمل الدابة على الذهاب كرهاً، فصار فعلها مضافاً إلى المكره، وكذلك مسألة الشهادة؛ لأن القاضي كالبهيمة محمول على القضاء بعد إقامة البينة كذا في "الفصول". يضاف إلى السوق لأن الدابة تسير على طبع السائق، ولهذا تقف بإيقافه وتسير بسيره، فصار فعلها مضافاً إلى السائق كذا في "المعدن". يُضاف إلى الشهادة: لأنه لما شبهت العلة بالسبب فيكون السبب بمعنى العلة، فيضاف إلى الشهادة. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ٢٣٦] بعد ظهور الحق إلخ فيه إيماء إلى أن فعل القضاء من القاضي وإن كان فعلاً اختيارياً صادراً من العبد المختار باختياره، فكان ينبغي أن يضاف حكم ضمان المال بضياعه إلى فعل القضاء و لم يضمنه الشهود؛ لما أن شهادتهم سبب محض كما في الدلالة، إلا أن القاضي لما اعتبر عند الشارع عاجزاً مجبوراً من حيث لا يسعه على مقتضى الشرع غير القضاء على حسب شهادة الشهود بعد تعديلهم وتزكيتهم، عد فعله بهذا النظر فعلاً غير اختياري في الملاحظة الشرعية، وصار حكمه حكم فعل البهيمة في عدم صلوح إضافة الحكم إليه، هذا البيان في الشهادة، وأما في التزكية، فإذا رجع المزكون عن التزكية فعند الإمام الأعظم : يضمنان المال بهذا الوجه، وعندهما: لا، فإنهم أثنوا على مسلم، والثناء ليس سبباً للتلف، وليست علته إلا قضاء القاضي وهو مختار في قضائه على أن رجوعهم لا يستلزم كذب الشهود، فلا يضاف التلف إلى رجوعهم عن التزكية أصله كذا في "الحصول".
The fourth research on qiyas. Chapter on the cause (sabab) of the ruling, its effective cause ('illa), and its condition. This is contrary to the depositary: if he guides the thief to the deposit and he steals it, or if a muhrim guides another to game in the sanctuary and he kills it; because the obligation of liability on the depositary is due to neglecting the required preservation, not due to the guidance; and on the muhrim because the guidance is a prohibition of his ihram, akin to applying perfume and wearing stitched garments, so he is liable for committing the prohibition, not for the guidance, except that the injury is established by the actual killing; before that, there is no ruling. The permissibility of the injury's effect rising is like healing in the chapter of wounds. And sometimes the sabab is in the meaning of 'illa, so the ruling is attributed to it. That is contrary to the depositary etc.: answer to a question. The result: liability on the depositary is due to his own direct injury, not by causation via the guided person; liability on the muhrim is due to committing a prohibited act. The exception: the injury is established by the actual killing. The like of healing: the wound after recovery does not show a trace of defect. And sometimes the sabab is treated as 'illa. Example: when the 'illa is established by the sabab, so the sabab is in the meaning of 'illa. For this we say: if someone drives an animal and it destroys something, the driver is liable. And if a witness by his testimony destroys wealth and then it appears false by his retraction, he is liable; because the animal's movement is attributed to the driving, and the judge's ruling is attributed to the testimony; because he cannot leave the ruling after the truth appears by the testimony of a just witness. Know that Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi divided the sabab into: pure sabab with no semblance of 'illa, like digging a well; figurative sabab with semblance of 'illa, like an oath for expiation; and sabab that is in the ruling 'illa, like the 'illa of the 'illa when attribution to the 'illa is impossible, such as driving and leading. He considered the last as sabab. He divided 'illa into seven types: by name, ruling, and meaning. The driver is liable because the animal's injury is caused by his coercion. The witness case: the judge is like an animal, compelled to rule after testimony. [Marginal notes] After the appearance of truth, the judge's act is considered involuntary in shari'a, so his act is like an animal's act. As for tazkiya (attestation): if the attestors retract, according to Imam A'zam they are liable for the wealth; according to the two, they are not, because they merely praised a Muslim, and praise is not a cause of loss.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion on the concepts of sabab (cause) and 'illa (effective cause) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, specifically within the framework of qiyas. The text begins by contrasting the ruling of a depositary who guides a thief with that of a muhrim who guides a hunter. The key point is that the depositary's liability arises from his own breach of duty (direct negligence), not from the guidance itself, while the muhrim's liability is due to violating the prohibitions of ihram, even though the actual killing is done by another. This illustrates the principle that a pure sabab (mere cause) does not attract liability unless it directly leads to the harm via a specific duty. The text then discusses scenarios where the sabab takes on the meaning of 'illa, such as in driving an animal or a witness's testimony. In these cases, the effect is attributed to the apparent cause (driver, witness) because the immediate actor (animal, judge) is considered compelled. The passage also cites Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi's classification of sabab into three categories and notes a disagreement with the author of al-Manar regarding whether certain causes are classified as sabab or 'illa. Finally, it addresses the specific case of tazkiya (attestation of witnesses' integrity), where Imam Abu Hanifa holds the attestors liable if they retract, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, as mere praise is not a cause of loss.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A cause that leads to a ruling without being the direct effective cause; it may be pure, figurative, or like 'illa
علة ('illa): The effective cause that directly necessitates the ruling; the 'illa is established by the sabab in some cases
شرط (shart): A condition that is necessary for the ruling but not part of the cause
ضممان (daman): Liability or guarantee for loss or destruction of property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, why is the driver of an animal liable for destruction caused by the animal?
A) Because the animal is considered the direct agent.
B) Because the driver's driving is the 'illa for the destruction.
C) Because the driver's act of driving coerces the animal, so the animal's act is attributed to the driver.
D) Because the driver owns the animal.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a pure sabab does not create liability by itself; liability arises when the sabab is treated as 'illa due to compulsion or when it involves a direct breach of duty.

Understanding Sabab: Definition, Types, and Attribution in Hanafi Usul
Defining sabab and its three types with legal examples and a fiqh dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify sabab into its three types according to al-Nasafi, explain how rulings are attributed to sabab in the absence of direct illah, and analyze the Hanafi dispute on tazkiya liability using the concept of sabab.

Core Idea
Sabab is the apparent cause that substitutes for the illah; knowing its three types is key to understanding attribution of rulings.

In Hanafi usul, the distinction between sabab (cause) and illah (effective cause) is crucial for attributing rulings. This passage from al-Nasafi's work classifies sabab into three types and demonstrates how rulings can be attributed to sabab when the true illah is inaccessible. It also includes a fiqh dispute about witness testimony and tazkiya that hinges on this principle, showing its practical importance.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Sabab from Illah
Read the opening lines where the author explains that sabab can take the meaning of illah when the illah is established via sabab. Understand the hierarchical relationship.
Sabab is a broader concept; illah is the direct effective cause.
2
Identify al-Nasafi's Three Types of Sabab
From the passage, list the three categories: pure sabab (mahd), metaphorical sabab (majazi), and sabab in the ruling of illah. Attach the examples given.
Memorize these for fatwa and qiyas analysis.
3
Analyze the Driver and Witness Examples
Trace the reasoning: the driver is liable because the animal's movement is attributed to his driving i.e., driving as sabab. Similarly, the witness is liable because the judge's ruling is attributed to testimony. Understand why the judge is considered compelled.
These illustrate how sabab becomes the basis for attribution.
4
Unpack the Tazkiya Dispute
Read the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Notice how it centers on whether tazkiya is a sabab that triggers liability upon retraction.
Abu Hanifa extends the sabab logic; the two limit it.
5
Apply the Sabab Classification to the Dispute
Identify which type of sabab tazkiya would fall under according to each view. Relate to the pure vs. metaphorical distinction.
This connects theory to a real ikhtilaf.

البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه
ومثاله: فيما يثبت العلةُ بالسبب، فيكون السبب في معنى العلة؛ لأنه لما ثبت العلةُ كون السبب بمعنى العلة بالسبب فيكون السبب في معنى علة العلة، فيُضاف الحكم إليه.

ولهذا قلنا: إذا ساق دابَّةً فأتلف شيئًا ضمن السائق. والشاهدُ إذا أتلف بشهادته مالاً فظَهَرَ بطلانها بالرجوع ضمن؛ لأن سير الدابَّة يضاف إلى السوق. وقضاء القاضي يُضاف إلى الشهادة؛ لما أنَّه لا يسعه ترك القضاء بعد ظهور الحق بشهادة العدل عنده، القاضي القاضي فيكون السبب : اعلم أن حافظ الدين النسفي قسم السبب إلى سبب محض ليس له شبهة العلية كحفر البئر، والدلالة على مال إنسان أو نفسه، وإلى سبب مجازي له شبهة العلة كاليمين للكفارة وتعليق الطلاق والعتاق للوقوع، وإلى سبب في الحكم العلة كعلة العلة عند تعذر الإضافة أي العلة كالسوق والقود، فأعتبر الأخير من الأسباب أيضاً، وقسم العلة إلى سبعة أقسام اسماً وحكماً ومعنى. ضمن السائقُ لأن إصابة يدها بذهابها وإن كان علة للتلف لكنها حدثت بالسوق؛ لأن السوق يحمل الدابة على الذهاب كرهاً، فصار فعلها مضافاً إلى المكره، وكذلك مسألة الشهادة؛ لأن القاضي كالبهيمة محمول على القضاء بعد إقامة البينة كذا في "الفصول". يضاف إلى السوق لأن الدابة تسير على طبع السائق، ولهذا تقف بإيقافه وتسير بسيره، فصار فعلها مضافاً إلى السائق كذا في "المعدن". يُضاف إلى الشهادة: لأنه لما شبهت العلة بالسبب فيكون السبب بمعنى العلة، فيضاف إلى الشهادة. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ٢٣٦] بعد ظهور الحق إلخ فيه إيماء إلى أن فعل القضاء من القاضي وإن كان فعلاً اختيارياً صادراً من العبد المختار باختياره، فكان ينبغي أن يضاف حكم ضمان المال بضياعه إلى فعل القضاء و لم يضمنه الشهود؛ لما أن شهادتهم سبب محض كما في الدلالة، إلا أن القاضي لما اعتبر عند الشارع عاجزاً مجبوراً من حيث لا يسعه على مقتضى الشرع غير القضاء على حسب شهادة الشهود بعد تعديلهم وتزكيتهم، عد فعله بهذا النظر فعلاً غير اختياري في الملاحظة الشرعية، وصار حكمه حكم فعل البهيمة في عدم صلوح إضافة الحكم إليه، هذا البيان في الشهادة، وأما في التزكية، فإذا رجع المزكون عن التزكية فعند الإمام الأعظم : يضمنان المال بهذا الوجه، وعندهما: لا، فإنهم أثنوا على مسلم، والثناء ليس سبباً للتلف، وليست علته إلا قضاء القاضي وهو مختار في قضائه على أن رجوعهم لا يستلزم كذب الشهود، فلا يضاف التلف إلى رجوعهم عن التزكية أصله كذا في "الحصول".
The Fourth Research on Qiyas. Chapter on the cause (sabab) of the ruling, its effective cause (illah), and its condition (shart). And its example: regarding the establishment of the illah by the sabab, so the sabab is in the sense of the illah; because when the illah is established by the sabab, then the sabab becomes in the sense of the illah of the illah, so the ruling is attributed to it. For this reason we said: if someone drives an animal and it destroys something, the driver is liable. And the witness, if by his testimony he destroys wealth and then the falsity of his testimony becomes clear by his retraction, he is liable; because the movement of the animal is attributed to the driving. And the judge's ruling is attributed to the testimony; because he cannot avoid ruling after the truth appears by the testimony of a just witness before him. So the sabab: Know that Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi divided the sabab into: a pure sabab that has no semblance of illah, like digging a well, and guiding to someone's property or life; a metaphorical sabab that has a semblance of illah, like the oath for expiation and the suspension of divorce and manumission for occurrence; and a sabab that is in the ruling of the illah like the illah of the illah when attribution is impossible, i.e., the illah like driving and leading. So he considered the last as one of the sababs as well, and he divided the illah into seven types: name, ruling, and meaning. The driver is liable because the injury of its leg by its movement, although it is the illah for destruction, happened due to the driving; because the driving compels the animal to go, so its action became attributed to the coercer. Similarly is the case of testimony; because the judge is like an animal compelled to ruling after the evidence is established, as in 'al-Fusul'. It is attributed to the driving because the animal moves according to the driver's nature, and for this it stops when he stops and moves when he moves, so its action became attributed to the driver, as in 'al-Ma'din'. It is attributed to the testimony: because when the illah is likened to the sabab, then the sabab is in the sense of the illah, so it is attributed to the testimony. [Umda al-Hawashi: p.236] 'After the truth appears etc.' implies that the act of the judge, although it is a voluntary act from the free agent by his choice, so it should be that the ruling of liability for the loss of wealth is attributed to the act of judging and the witnesses would not be liable; because their testimony is a pure cause as in guidance. However, because the judge is considered by the Lawgiver as incapable and compelled since he cannot, according to the dictates of the Law, do anything other than rule based on the witnesses' testimony after their tazkiya (declaration of integrity), his act in this regard is regarded as involuntary in the legal view, and its ruling became like the act of an animal in terms of the inability to attribute the ruling to it. This explanation is for testimony. As for tazkiya, when the ones who gave tazkiya retract from tazkiya, according to Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa): they both guarantee the wealth in this manner; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): no, because they merely praised a Muslim, and praising is not a cause for destruction, and its only illah is the judge's ruling, and he is free in his ruling. Moreover, their retraction does not entail the falsehood of the witnesses, so destruction is not attributed to their retraction from tazkiya. Its origin is as in 'al-Husul'.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is from the fourth section on qiyas, specifically a chapter defining the cause (sabab), its relation to the effective cause (illah), and its condition (shart). The author begins by explaining the relationship between sabab and illah: sometimes the illah is established through the sabab, so the sabab takes on the meaning of the illah, and the ruling is attributed to it. He gives legal examples: a driver who drives an animal that destroys property is liable because the destruction is attributed to his driving, even though the direct cause is the animal's movement. Similarly, a witness who gives false testimony that leads to loss of wealth becomes liable upon retraction because the judge's ruling is attributed to the testimony, as the judge is considered compelled in his ruling. The author then cites al-Nasafi's classification of sabab into three types: (1) pure sabab with no semblance of illah (e.g., digging a well), (2) metaphorical sabab with semblance of illah (e.g., an oath for expiation), and (3) sabab in the sense of illah (e.g., driving). The passage further explains the rationale for attribution in both cases and ends with a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the liability of those who perform tazkiya (declaration of witness integrity) if they retract. According to Abu Hanifa, they are liable because their tazkiya is akin to a cause; according to the two, they are not because praise is not a cause for destruction.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The apparent cause that leads to a ruling, often used in place of the illah when the illah is inaccessible.
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause that directly necessitates the ruling.
سبب محض (sabab mahd): A pure cause that has no semblance of illah, e.g., digging a well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi's classification, which type of sabab has a semblance of illah?
A) Sabab mahd
B) Sabab majazi
C) Sabab fi hukm al-illah
D) Sabab muqayyad

Key Takeaway
The concept of sabab is fundamental in Hanafi usul for attributing rulings when the direct illah is unknown; its three types cover pure, metaphorical, and illah-substitute causes.

The Sabab Standing in Place of the Illah: A Principle of Ease in Hanafi Usul
Explanation of the usul rule: sabab stands in for illah when illah is inaccessible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul principle of iqamat al-sabab maqam al-illah and apply it to identify the sabab and illah in given fiqh examples.

Core Idea
When the true cause is hidden, the Lawgiver places a manifest sign in its stead for ease.

In the Hanafi legal tradition, not every ruling is tied to a directly observable cause. Sometimes the true effective cause (illah) is hidden or difficult to ascertain. To ease the burden on the obligated person, the Lawgiver establishes a manifest cause (sabab) that stands in for the illah. This lesson unpacks that principle through three classical examples: sleep nullifying wudu, valid seclusion entailing full mahr and iddah, and travel triggering legal concessions.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Clearly articulate the rule: when knowledge of the true illah is impossible, the sabab is set in its place, and the ruling revolves around the sabab.
This is a principle of ease (taysir), not a replacement of illah when illuminable.
2
Identify the Components in Each Example
For each example (sleep, seclusion, travel), identify what serves as the illah (hidden cause) and what serves as the sabab (manifest cause).
Illah: hadath (ritual impurity), actual intercourse, true hardship. Sabab: complete sleep, valid seclusion, travel.
3
Explain the Rationale
Explain why the illah is considered inaccessible in each case: sleep makes detection of emission impossible; true hardship is subjective and varies by person; actual intercourse may not be verifiable.
The sabab is chosen because it is easily observable and reliably indicates the illah in most cases.
4
Recognize the Scope
Understand that this principle applies only where the illah is genuinely inaccessible; if the illah can be known, it takes precedence over the sabab.
For example, if someone consciously breaks wudu by passing wind, the illah (hadath) is known, so the sabab (sleep) is irrelevant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه
ثم السَّببُ قد يقام مقام العلة عند تعذر الإطلاع على حقيقة العلة تيسيراً للأمر على المكلّف، ويسقط به اعتبار العلة، ويُدار الحكم على السبب. وجوداً وعدماً ومثاله في الشرعيَّات: النومُ الكامل؛ فإنه لما أُقيمَ مقامَ الحدث، سقَطَ اعتبار حقيقة الحدث ويدارُ الانتقاض على كمال النوم. وكذلك الخَلْوَةُ الصحيحة لما أقيمَتْ مقامَ الوطء سقط اعتبار حقيقة الوطء، فيُدَار الحكم على صحة الخلوة في حق كمال المهر ولزوم العدة. وكذلك السفَرُ لما أُقيمَ مقامَ المشقة في حق الرخصة سقط اعتبار حقيقة المشقة، ويُدَار الحكم على السبب. يعني على العمل بحقيقة العلة من الحرج، فلذا سقط اعتبار العلة. أُقيم مقامَ الحدث: لانتفاض الطهارة؛ لأنه سبب لانتفاضها؛ لأن النوم لا يخلو عن خروج شيء عادة والعلة الحدث، والإطلاع على وجود الحدث في حالة النوم متعذر، والنوم لاشتماله على استرخاء المفاصل داع إلى وجود الحدث، فيكون وجوده حادثاً بالنوم، فأقيم مقام الحدث، فلا يرد ما يتوهم أن الوضوء كان ثابتاً بيقين وفي النوم خروج النجاسة مشكوك؛ لأن الشارع أقام نفس النوم مقام حقيقة خروج النجاسة كذا في بعض الحواشي. وكذلك الخَلْوَةُ إلخ إي إذا خلا الزوج بامرأة وليس هناك مانع من الوطء لا شرعاً ولا حساً ولا طبعاً كصوم (هو مانع وطء شرعاً) ومرض (هو) مانع وطء حساً) وحيض هو مانع وطء طبعاً وشرعاً) كأنه وطئها إقامة الخلوة الصحيحة مقام الوطء، ولذا سقط اعتبار حقيقة الوطء ويدار الحكم هو وجوب المهر والعدة وغيرهما) على صحة الخلوة بأن لم يوجد (مانع فيجب المهر الكامل ويلزم العدة وإن تيقن أنه ما كان بينهما وطء بأن كانت بكراً بعد الخلوة الصحيحة إلخ: أي الخالية عن الموانع الحسية والشرعية أقيمت مقام الوطء، والأخبار والآثار فيه كثيرة من طريق مختلف لو لا ما يمنعنا من ضيق المقام لأوردناها. مقام المشقة: لتعذر الإطلاع على حقيقة المشقة؛ لأنها أمر مبطن يتفاوت أحوال الناس فيه.
Chapter on the cause, its effective cause, and its condition. Then the sabab may be set in place of the illah when knowledge of the true illah is impossible, for ease upon the obligated person, and consideration of the illah is dropped, and the ruling is made to revolve on the sabab, both in existence and non-existence. Its example in the religious matters: complete sleep; because when it is set in place of the hadath (ritual impurity), consideration of the true hadath is dropped, and the nullification (of ablution) is made to revolve on complete sleep. Similarly, valid seclusion (khalwa) when it is set in place of intercourse, consideration of true intercourse is dropped, so the ruling revolves on the validity of seclusion regarding the complete dower and the obligation of waiting period. Similarly, travel when it is set in place of hardship concerning concessions, consideration of true hardship is dropped, and the ruling is made to revolve on the sabab. Meaning: because in obligation there is difficulty regarding acting on the true illah, so consideration of the illah is dropped. It was set in place of hadath: regarding the nullification of ablution; because it is a cause for its nullification; because sleep is not normally free from some emission, and the illah is hadath, and knowledge of the existence of hadath during sleep is impossible, and sleep, because it involves relaxation of joints, prompts the existence of hadath, so its existence occurs by sleep, so it was set in place of hadath. So there is no objection to the doubt that ablution was certain and during sleep the emission is doubtful; because the Lawgiver set sleep itself in place of the true emission of impurity, as in some glosses. Likewise, valid seclusion etc.: i.e., when a husband is alone with a woman and there is no impediment to intercourse, neither legally, nor physically, nor naturally, like fasting (which is a legal impediment), sickness (which is a physical impediment), menstruation (which is a natural and legal impediment), it is as if he had intercourse; the valid seclusion is set in place of intercourse, so consideration of true intercourse is dropped and the ruling revolves on the validity of seclusion: that when there is no impediment, the full dower is obligatory and the waiting period is required, even if it is certain that there was no intercourse, as if she were a virgin after valid seclusion etc.: i.e., seclusion free from physical and legal impediments is set in place of intercourse. The reports and traditions on this are many from various paths; were it not that lack of space prevents us, we would have presented them. In the place of hardship: because knowledge of true hardship is impossible; because it is an inward matter in which people's conditions vary.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental usul principle: when the true effective cause (illah) is inaccessible or difficult to determine, the Lawgiver may establish a manifest cause (sabab) in its place for the sake of ease. The ruling then revolves around the sabab rather than the hidden illah. The author provides three classical examples from Hanafi fiqh: (1) Sleep: sleep is set in place of the hadath (ritual impurity) because it is impossible to know if something actually exited during sleep. Thus, complete sleep nullifies wudu, even if no emission is detected. (2) Valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha): when a husband and wife are alone without any impediment (legal, physical, or natural), valid seclusion is set in place of actual intercourse. Therefore, the full mahr and iddah become obligatory even if intercourse did not occur. (3) Travel: travel is set in place of hardship for concessions (rukhsas) like shortening prayers and breaking fast, because true hardship varies and is difficult to assess. The commentary clarifies that the reason for this substitution is to avoid hardship (haraj) in obligating discerning the true illah.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The manifest cause that is set in place of the hidden illah for ease.
العلة (al-illah): The true effective cause that is hidden or difficult to know.
النوم الكامل (al-nawm al-kamil): Complete sleep, which nullifies wudu according to the Hanafi school, set in place of hadath.
الخلوة الصحيحة (al-khalwah al-sahihah): Valid seclusion between spouses free from any impediment to intercourse (legal, physical, or natural).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is travel set as a sabab for legal concessions (rukhsas) like shortening prayer?
A) Because travel itself is a hardship.
B) Because the true hardship is subjective and difficult to measure.
C) Because travelers are always in a state of hardship.
D) Because the Lawgiver wants to discourage travel.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle of iqamat al-sabab maqam al-illah allows rulings to be based on observable causes when the true effective cause is inaccessible, serving the objective of ease in the law.

Substituting Sabab for 'Illa When the 'Illa is Hidden
Explains the principle of sabab replacing 'illa with three fiqh examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle of substituting sabab for 'illa when the 'illa is hidden and apply it to the three given fiqh examples (sleep, khalwa, travel).

Core Idea
When the true cause ('illa) is hidden, the Shari'ah substitutes the observable cause (sabab) to ease the ruling.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between sabab (cause) and 'illa (effective cause). In many rulings, the true 'illa is not directly accessible, so the Lawgiver makes the ruling revolve around a visible sabab instead. This lesson examines this principle using three classic fiqh examples from Usul al-Shashi, highlighting how the substitution operates and what conditions (shurut) are attached.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Identify the general rule from the first sentence: sabab stands in place of 'illa when the 'illa is hidden, to avoid hardship. Note that the ruling is then attached to the sabab.
The rationale is taysir (ease) for the mukallaf.
2
Analyze the Sleep Example
Understand that complete sleep substitutes for the hidden hadath (impurity). The nullification of wudu revolves around sleep, not the actual (unknown) impurity. Condition: sleep must be complete (kamil).
This is the first of three Shar'iyyat examples.
3
Analyze the Khalwa Example
Valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) substitutes for actual intercourse. Full mahr and 'iddah are required even if no intercourse occurred, provided there are no barriers (legal, physical, natural).
Barriers include fasting (legal), sickness (physical), menstruation (natural/legal).
4
Analyze the Travel Example
Travel substitutes for the hidden hardship (mashaqqa). The licenses of qasr and iftar are attached to travel itself, not to the degree of hardship. Condition: intent to travel the required distance.
The sultan example shows that even a ruler touring his kingdom may claim licenses if he intends the distance.
5
Identify the Common Thread
All three examples illustrate the same principle: substitution when the true 'illa is hidden. Each sabab has its own shurut (conditions) that must be met for the ruling to apply.
The commentary expands on each condition and addresses potential objections.

[عمدة الحواشي: ص ٢٢٦] على السبب لما أن في التكليف يعني على العمل بحقيقة العلة من الحرج، فلذا سقط اعتبار العلة. أُقيم مقَامَ الحدث: لانتفاض الطهارة؛ لأنه سبب لانتفاضها؛ لأن النوم لا يخلو عن خروج شيء عادة والعلة الحدث، والإطلاع على وجود الحدث في حالة النوم متعذر، والنوم لاشتماله على استرخاء المفاصل داع إلى وجود الحدث، فيكون وجوده حادثاً بالنوم، فأقيم مقام الحدث، فلا يرد ما يتوهم أن الوضوء كان ثابتاً بيقين وفي النوم خروج النجاسة مشكوك؛ لأن الشارع أقام نفس النوم مقام حقيقة خروج النجاسة كذا في بعض الحواشي. وكذلك الخَلْوَةُ إلخ إي إذا خلا الزوج بامرأة وليس هناك مانع من الوطء لا شرعاً ولا حساً ولا طبعاً كصوم (هو مانع وطء شرعاً) ومرض (هو) مانع وطء حساً) وحيض هو مانع وطء طبعاً وشرعاً) كأنه وطئها إقامة الخلوة الصحيحة مقام الوطء، ولذا سقط اعتبار حقيقة الوطء ويدار الحكم هو وجوب المهر والعدة وغيرهما) على صحة الخلوة بأن لم يوجد (مانع فيجب المهر الكامل ويلزم العدة وإن تيقن أنه ما كان بينهما وطء بأن كانت بكراً بعد الخلوة الصحيحة إلخ: أي الخالية عن الموانع الحسية والشرعية أقيمت مقام الوطء، والأخبار والآثار فيه كثيرة من طريق مختلف لو لا ما يمنعنا من ضيق المقام لأوردناها. مقام المشقة: لتعذر الإطلاع على حقيقة المشقة؛ لأنها أمر مبطن يتفاوت أحوال الناس فيه.
الحكم على نفس السفر، حتى أن السلطان لو طاف في أطراف مملكته يقصد به مقدار السفر، كان له الرخصة في الإفطار والقصر.
[عمدة الحواشي: ص ۲۲۸] يقصد به مقدار إلخ مقدار السفر وهو سير ثلاثة أيام وليالها، وإنما قيد بقصد مقدار السفر؛ لأنه لو طاف سنين: و لم يقصد به مسيرة ثلاثة أيام ولياليها لم تكن له الرخصة.
Chapter on the cause (sabab) of the ruling, its effective cause ('illa), and its condition (shart). Then: the sabab may stand in the place of the 'illa when ascertaining the true 'illa is impossible, to make matters easy for the obligated person, and thereby consideration of the 'illa falls away, and the ruling is made to revolve around the sabab, both in existence and non-existence. An example in the Shar'iyyat: complete sleep; since it was made to stand in the place of hadath (ritual impurity), consideration of the true hadath fell away, and the nullification (of wudu) is made to revolve around complete sleep. Likewise, valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) when it was made to stand in the place of intercourse, consideration of the true intercourse fell away, so the ruling is made to revolve around the validity of seclusion regarding the full dower and the necessity of 'iddah. Likewise, travel when it was made to stand in the place of hardship regarding licenses, consideration of the true hardship fell away, and the ruling is made to revolve around travel itself, so much so that if the sultan tours the extremities of his kingdom intending the distance of travel, he is entitled to the license of breaking fast and shortening prayer. [Commentary] ... The ruling is upon travel itself, so that if the sultan tours... intending the distance of travel, he has the license of iftar and qasr.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a chapter on the relationship between sabab (cause), 'illa (effective cause), and shart (condition) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author states a key principle: when the true 'illa is difficult to ascertain, the Shari'ah substitutes the sabab for the 'illa to avoid hardship. This substitution means the ruling is now attached directly to the sabab, not to the hidden 'illa. Three examples are given: 1) Complete sleep: Sleep is the sabab for wudu nullification because it typically leads to impurity, but since actual impurity is hidden, the sabab (sleep) replaces the 'illa (hadath). 2) Valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha): In Hanafi fiqh, if a husband and wife are alone with no legal, physical, or natural barriers, it is treated like actual intercourse for the purposes of full mahr and 'iddah, even if no intercourse occurred. The sabab (seclusion) replaces the 'illa (actual intercourse). 3) Travel: Travel is the sabab for licenses like qasr and iftar, replacing the 'illa of hardship which is internal and varies. The commentary expands on each, noting that the substitution is due to difficulty in discovering the 'illa, and that condition like intent (qasd) affects the ruling (e.g., the sultan must intend travel distance).

Key Terms
السبب (as-sabab): The observable, concrete cause that stands in for the hidden 'illa for ease; the ruling is made to revolve around the sabab.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause (ratio legis) of a ruling; in this context, it is the true but hidden cause that is replaced by the sabab.
الشرط (ash-shart): A condition that must be present for the sabab to be effective (e.g., khalwa must be free of barriers).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because sleep is the true 'illa of nullification.
B) Because the release of impurities is hidden during sleep, so sleep is made the sabab to ease the ruling.
C) Because sleep always causes impurity to exit.
D) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly stated that sleep breaks wudu.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that sabab replaces 'illa when the latter is hidden allows rulings to be based on observable phenomena, ensuring legal ease.
